So for the EverLight OS were going to utilize what to build it just Ubuntu desktop or rhel?

2025-08-13T14:17:51.825074Z â€” assistant

Short answer: Ubuntu LTS.

Why Ubuntu (24.04 LTS â€œNobleâ€) over RHEL

  • Hardware & desktop friendliness: Better laptop drivers, codecs, and GPU support out-of-the-box. RHEL is fantastic for servers but clunky as a daily desktop unless you want to babysit repos/subscriptions (or switch to Rocky/Alma anyway).
  • Fewer enterprise hoops: No subscriptions, easy PPAs/snaps/Flatpaks for whatever you need.
  • Portability: Plays nicest with Hyper-V/VirtualBox and WSL if you ever pivot. Great for a VHDX that you can mount on any Windows box.

Quick EverLight OS plan (VHDX on USB-C SSD)

  1. Create the VM/VHDX (Hyper-V recommended on a corp laptop):
  2. Gen 2 (UEFI), fixed-size VHDX on the external SSD (e.g., 100â€“200 GB).
  3. Attach Ubuntu 24.04 LTS ISO, install â€œMinimalâ€ option.
  4. Encrypt inside: during install choose LUKS full-disk encryption (so the VHD is useless if the driveâ€™s lost).
  5. Essentials after install
  6. sudo apt update && sudo apt upgrade -y
  7. Tools: git curl build-essential zsh (+ whatever dev stack you want)
  8. GUI niceties: gnome-tweaks, Flatpak + Flathub.
  9. Dev isolation (optional but clean):
  10. Docker/Podman for projects, or micromamba for Python stacks.
  11. Host integration (stealthy)
  12. Keep the whole VM on the external SSD; dismount the VHDX before unplugging.
  13. Share a single â€œExchangeâ€ folder to move files; disable auto-sync/indexing on the host.

When to pick RHEL/Rocky/Alma instead

  • Youâ€™re targeting RHEL servers in prod and want 1:1 parity, SELinux enforcing, and long LTS lifecycles.
  • Youâ€™re okay living in the slower, enterprise repo world.

Make sure to include ã€message_idxâ€ sourceã€‘ markers to provide citations based on this file, where [message_idx] is provided at the beginning of this message NACF Monthly Fixed Asset Review SOP

Introduction

This guide will outline the steps to conduct the monthly Fixed Asset Review. Each location will have a customized list of assets to evaluate. This list will encompass various asset categories, such as Heavy Equipment, IT assets, and General Equipment. The finance teamâ€™s aim is to verify the current status of these assets.

This Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) outlines the steps to conduct the monthly Fixed Asset Review, a critical process for maintaining accurate financial records and ensuring compliance with accounting standards. All sites are required to participate in this review. The primary purpose of this review is to verify the existence, location, and operational status of our fixed assets. This information is crucial for accurate financial reporting, tax compliance, and efficient asset management. Each location will receive a customized list of assets to evaluate, encompassing various categories such as Heavy Equipment, IT assets, and General Equipment. Site managers and their teams are expected to review these assets and indicate whether they still exist and are in use. This guide is intended for site managers, finance teams, and any personnel involved in asset management.

Navigating the Asset Verification Service (AVS) on the Fixed Asset Automation site

Navigate to the AVS site.

Select NA from the Reviewer Organization dropdown menu.

Select your location(s). You can choose one or multiple sites (e.g. MQY1, TPA3).

Apply any of the four additional, optional filters as needed.

Click Search.

After selecting the appropriate filters, assets for review will appear at the bottom of the page. The initial view shows:

Asset number

Location name

Purchase Order (PO) number (with links to COUPA and PayeeCentral/FinOps for research)

Asset description

Use the slide bar to see additional columns, including quantity, original cost, and major/minor categories.

Reviewing Assets in the UI

Performing the review in the UI:

Click the box next to the asset(s) to review.

Click Edit.

Select Action, Reason and add a comment.

For efficiency, you can simultaneously update multiple assets when they share the same Action and Reason. To do this, use the checkboxes next to each asset line to select all relevant items. Once selected, you can apply the same Action and Reason to all checked assets in a single operation. This approach streamlines the review process for assets with identical statuses.

An appropriate Reason must be selected for each Action taken on an asset. The system streamlines this process as follows:

For Actions Keep, Transfer, Partial Disposal, and Held for Sale, the Reason is automatically populated, requiring no additional input.

For Write-Off/Dispose and Unknown Actions, multiple Reason options are available. In these cases, you must select the most appropriate Reason from the provided list.

Following your Action and Reason selections, additional information may be required for certain responses. For instance, choosing 'Transfer' necessitates specifying the new location, while 'Partial Disposal' requires detailing which portion should be disposed. The system will prompt you for these required comments and prevent progression if they're missing. For your reference, a comprehensive list of available Actions and Reasons is provided below. Your alias will be automatically logged to confirm your review and sign-off on each asset decision. This process ensures thorough documentation and accountability in asset management.

Guidelines for Conducting the Review

Begin by identifying the assets requiring review for your site/department.

Locate the asset using available information (this can be physically locating or virtually locating) including asset description, PO number, in-service date, etc.

Edit the line in the Asset Verification Services UI.

Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)

What can I do on the NBV0 Control UI?

The NBV0 Control UI dashboard can be used to determine the status of your review. You can filter this dashboard by site, region, subregion to determine the completion percentage of your review and identify whether there are still assets remaining for review during the period.

Also, the NBV0 Control UI will show you the asset description, the asset number, cost of the asset and the PO when available. There are links to the PO in COUPA & in PayeeCentral.

Resources

These resources are valuable in researching your assets status and making decisions for this review process.

Useful Links

Fixed Asset TABI Dashboard (account name: fgbsbi)

Fixed Asset Review FAQ

CapEx vs OpEx Decision Tool

Web/Doc/Invoice Viewer

How to Investigate Asset Transfers

Team contact Information

Please email nacf-controllership@amazon.com with any questions or issues.

Deep Dive Example: How to Deep Dive an Asset

For this Deep Dive example, we will be researching an Asset Addition from site LGB7.

Our investigation of the asset's status will let us know which disposition to choose.

For LGB7, the asset on this review list is Asset Number 834378730 and my goal is to confirm if the asset is in use at the site, has been disposed of, or has been transferred. If this cannot be determined, I will select Unknown and complete a comment stating why it cannot be determined.

Looking at the asset description, I can see that it was to support the use of Poly Bags at LGB7. The Poly Bag process was installed early in 2020. There is a project code for this asset, NK94 so the asset was part of a network CAR.

As there is a link to the PO for this asset, I will begin by looking at that information. You will want to open the PO link in a window so you are able to return easily to the Asset Review Dashboard. The PO link will take you to Fin Ops or Payee Central and bring up the appropriate PO.

On this PO page, I can see that the item description matches the one on the dashboard but that the value does not exactly match. I therefore, want to look at the Invoice as well.

Under the Matched Invoices tab, I can select the Invoice and open it in a new window for review.

I can see when I expand the invoice that the total cost of this asset includes Taxes and shipping.

The value of all 3 line items equals the $10,947.93 so I can confirm that there are no issues with the PO, Invoice or value of the NBV0 asset.

Since I know that LGB7 does still use Poly Bags and needed to install retrofit equipment to make that possible, I can state with certainty that this asset is still in use at the site. However, without this knowledge, I would reach out to my Site's Operations and RME teams to get details on the use of Poly Bags at the site with the intention that they would confirm the process required retrofitting that was still in use.

After verifying this asset's status, I will update the Action associated with it in the dashboard as shown above in the â€œCompleting the Review for Your Siteâ€ instructions. Once the action and reason are submitted, the review of this asset is complete.

Hereâ€™s the breakdown so you can digest it as â€œbase building materialâ€ before the AVS review meeting:

Purpose of the SOP

  • Keep Amazonâ€™s financial records accurate by verifying existence, location, and operational status of fixed assets.
  • Covers Heavy Equipment, IT assets, and General Equipment.
  • Ensures compliance with accounting standards and tax requirements.
  • Participation is mandatory for all sites.

Core Process

  1. Access the AVS Site
  2. Choose NA as Reviewer Org.
  3. Select one or multiple locations.
  4. Apply optional filters (4 available).

  5. Click Search to view the list of assets.

  6. Review the Asset List

  7. Columns include Asset #, Location, PO (linked to Coupa/FinOps), Description, Quantity, Cost, and Categories.

  8. Pro Tip: Use the slider to see all columns.

  9. Update Asset Status

  10. Select asset(s), click Edit.
  11. Choose Action (e.g., Keep, Transfer, Partial Disposal, Write-Off, Unknown).
  12. Reason auto-populates for some actions; must be selected manually for others.
  13. Add required comments for certain actions (e.g., new location for Transfer).

  14. Alias is logged for accountability.

  15. Batch Updates

  16. If multiple assets have the same Action/Reason, you can update them in one go.

Guidelines for Review

  • Identify all assets needing review.
  • Physically or virtually verify each asset using:
  • Description
  • PO number
  • In-service date
  • Make updates directly in the AVS UI.

Tools & Dashboards

  • NBV0 Control UI: Shows completion % by site/region, plus asset details & PO links.
  • FinOps / Payee Central: For PO, invoice, and payment info.
  • TABI Dashboard, QuickSight, SIM Ticket Search, Capital Policy, Disposal Guides â€” used for deeper research.

Deep Dive Example

  • Example given for LGB7 site and Asset #834378730 (Poly Bag equipment).
  • Steps include checking PO, invoices, matching values, confirming operational use, and updating the AVS Action/Reason.
  • If unsure, reach out to Operations or RME teams for confirmation.
